## 9.13 Always-On Cluster (AON) and SPE
### 9.13.1 Overview
The AON cluster provides a processor (the SPE) and a set of peripherals in a small power island that supports some I/O functions, and also provides hardware to wake the SoC when a number of different events occur. Use cases include, but are not limited to: low power sensor management during standby running specific communications stacks in standby, including the CAN bus wake management from sleep states The cluster consists of an ARM Cortex®-R5F processor core with a tightly coupled RAM, supporting peripherals (such as timers and an interrupt controller), various I/O controller peripherals, a DMA engine, an inter-connect fabric, and the logic to manage the cluster power states and wake sensing feature.

Always-On Cluster (AON) and SPE The Cortex-R5F processor in the AON cluster is also referred to as the SPE, an abbreviation for its mobile role as the Sensor Processing Engine. For brevity, the Cortex-R5F core used in AON is referred to as Cortex-R5 or just R5, but does include the Floating Point and Double Precision Floating Point capabilities. While the Cortex-R5 may be used for the use cases outlined above, it is actually a generic CPU able to run arbitrary software. Nothing in the hardware design limits usage to just those applications.
#### 9.13.1.1 AON Cluster Diagram
The following figure shows the block diagram of the AON Cluster.
**Figure 9.96 AON Cluster Block Diagram**

AON Cluster Functional Description
### 9.13.2 AON Cluster Functional Description
#### 9.13.2.1 Cortex-R5 Processor
The Cortex-R5 processor supports the following features: ARMv7-R ISA Integrated instruction and data caches TCM interface for local SRAM Vectored interrupt support 64-bit AXI master interface for DRAM requests 32-bit AXI master interface for MMIO requests 32-bit AHB master interface for AVIC access AXI slave interface for DMA access to the local SRAM
#### 9.13.2.2 Processor Configuration
The AON Cluster Cortex-R5 is implemented with the following features: 32 KB instruction cache 32 KB data cache 256 KB of SRAM attached to TCMB as two banks of 128 KB SRAM TCMA base address set to 0 Init low vectors Processor version r1p3 Floating-Point Unit extensions including double-precision capability
#### 9.13.2.3 Interrupt Controller
The Cortex-R5 does not have an integrated interrupt controller. A pair of ARM PL192 vectored interrupt controllers on the local bus serve as the interrupt controller for the AON Cortex-R5. The SoC implements PL192 version r0p0.
#### 9.13.2.4 Processor and Interrupt Controller Documentation
Detailed documentation for the Cortex-R5 Processor and the PL192 Interrupt Controller are readily available from ARM, and may be downloaded from the ARM web site. A good starting point is these documents:

AON Cluster Functional Description Document DDI 0273A This TRM assumes access to these documents, and does not reproduce information from them.
#### 9.13.2.5 Timers
The Cortex-R5 does not have any integrated timers. Timers for the AON Cluster are provided by a separate timer block in the AON Cluster.
#### 9.13.2.6 TCM Interface
Cortex-R5 provides two tightly coupled memory ports. These ports, named ATCM and BTCM are meant to provide low latency access to the Cortex-R5 processor. The ATCM hosts the EVP interface (see below) and the BTCM hosts a 256 KB RAM.
**Figure 9.97 Cortex-R5 TCM interface**
The following pin and build configurations define the ATCM and BTCM configurations.

AON Cluster Functional Description
#### 9.13.2.7 ATCM Interface
The Cortex-R5 ATCM interface hosts the Exception Vector Table module. The EVP is wrapped in the ATCM Wrapper that provides the ATCM interface to Cortex-R5.
##### 9.13.2.7.1 Exception Vector Pointers (EVP)
When Cortex-R5 takes an exception (including the reset exception), processor execution is forced to an address that corresponds to the type of exception. These addresses are called the exception vectors. By default, the exception vectors are eight consecutive word-aligned memory addresses, starting at an exception base address (which is reset default to 0x0000_0000 for the AON Cortex- R5 since VINITHI is tied to 0). The EVP module is implemented through a set of 16 registers starting at address 0x0. The table below shows the default organization of the EVP coming out of reset. The programmability of EVP allows the processor to jump to an arbitrary address space in the entire memory space that is accessible to the AON Cortex-R5. Table 9.98 EVP Register Table Offset Data Description 0x00 LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] Reset vector. According to the ARM Architecture manual, the PC reads an address equals current instruction + 8. 0x04 LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] Undefined exception 0x08 LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] SWI (also known as SVC) exception 0x0C LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] Prefetch abort 0x10 LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] Data abort 0x14 LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] Reserved 0x18 LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] IRQ 0x1C LDR, PC, [PC+0x18] FIQ 0x20 NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM TCMB Base Address 0x24 NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 4 0x28 NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 8 0x2C NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 12 0x30 NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 16 0x34 NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 20 0x38 NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 24

AON Cluster Functional Description Offset Data Description 0x3C NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM + 30 The EVP table above assumes that the TCMB starts at address NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM. The redirection of exception vectors enables BPMP to execute an ISR handler in the entire memory space accessible by it. The following steps are performed to handle EVP requests: 1. 2. The Cortex-R5 issues a read for exception vector address (@0x0000_00XX). EVP decodes exception vector aperture, and generates read-response. a. Returns LD PC, [PC + 0x18] instruction as return data. 3. This results in PC getting loaded with pointer to exception vector. Notes: 1. Cortex-R5 additionally supports vectored exception handling specifically for IRQ interrupts. This is supported in conjunction with the PL192 VIC interrupt controller. When an IRQ exception is triggered by the VIC, it can optionally send out a pointer to the interrupt handler to service that particular interrupt. In case of vectored interrupts through VIC, the EVP table is not referenced by the Cortex-R5. EVP in earlier chips supported vectorization of interrupts. This is deprecated since the required vectorization support is already provided through VIC interface. EVP reset is decoupled from the Cortex-R5 CPU reset. This enables the Cortex-R5 to be independently reset without affecting the content of EVP registers. 2. 3.
#### 9.13.2.8 Error Checking and Signaling
When access is not allowed by the ATCM interface, it signals an error. When bit[0] of the Auxiliary Control Register (ACTLR.ATCMECEN) is set to 1, the error triggers an undefined exception on Cortex-R5 accesses or AXI slave error on AXI slave requests by asserting the ATCERROR. ATCERROR is asserted when any of the following happens: ATCADDR address does not decode into the address space implemented within the ATCM wrapper. Whenever write access is made from the ARM ATCM interface to the ATCM. ATCLATEERROR is not used to trigger an error since the ATCLATEERROR response is discarded by the AXI slave interface.

AON Cluster Functional Description
#### 9.13.2.9 BTCM Interface
BTCM hosts the Cortex-R5 tightly coupled 256 KB RAM. BTCM is split internally into two ports, B0TCM and B1TCM. The address range for the BTCM is defined in the NV_ADDRESS_MAP_AON_BTCM define in the global AMAP. The BTCM has two ports for two reasons: One can be used by the processor and the other by the AON DMA. Cortex-R5 can work on one bank of the BTCM while AON DMA can page in data/code to/from the other. If the code and data space can be separated between B0TCM and B1TCM, then instruction and data accesses from Cortex-R5 can be done independently. 1. 2.
#### 9.13.2.10 BTCM RAM Configuration
The 128 KB of RAM on each BTCM channel is constructed of eight banks of 16 KB RAM. The BTCM RAM banks are logically configured into eight 32 KB power-gating groups. Since the BTCM interface is operating in interleaved mode one bank from B0TCM and one bank from B1TCM are in each power-gating group. Bank 0 starts at the bottom 32 KB of the BTCM address space.
#### 9.13.2.11 Error Checking and Signaling
Accesses to the BTCM signal an error when the particular access isn't allowed by BTCM interface. When bit 1 and bit 2 of the Auxiliary Control Register (ACTLR.B0TCMECEN and ACTLR.B1TCMECEN) are set to 1, the error triggers an undefined exception on Cortex-R5 accesses or AXI slave error on AXI slave requests by asserting the B0TCERROR or B1TCERROR. An error is asserted when any of the following occurs: The SD, SLP, or DSLP port for a TCM RAM bank is asserted and the TCM RAM bank is accessed.
#### 9.13.2.12 Interrupts
The interrupt sources from/to the SPE (Cortex-R5) in the AON block are comprised of the following components: {Vector/Scalar} interrupts are driven through a pair of daisy-chained ARM Vectored Interrupt Controllers (AVIC) 1. Specific peripherals such as TKE, DMA, etc., (which are exclusively owned by the SPE) have their interrupts connected to AVIC. Other I/O peripherals which can be owned by the SPE and other system masters, such as the CCPLEX, send their interrupts to AVIC as well as to top level LIC, depending on the usage model software can mask the interrupts in unused path.

AON Cluster Functional Description 2. Interrupts from the Legacy Interrupt Controller (LIC) that feed into the AVIC. There are four such interrupts coming from LIC. There are a few peripherals and interrupt sources connected to LIC can be managed by the SPE by properly enabling the routing to AON cluster channel in LIC and finally routing the aggregated interrupt to AVIC. 3. AON Interrupts to other Clusters There are a few peripherals that are controlled by other clusters though they are instanced in the AON cluster (e.g., CAN, UART). For example, specific instances of the UART have usage models where they are controlled by the Safety Cluster Engine (SCE) or the Boot and Power Management Processor (BPMP). These peripherals interrupt are connected to the AON cluster and to the other clusters apart from LIC; they are fanned out to LIC and other respective clusters. 4. Interrupts to AON from SoC Domain Peripherals UART6 and UART8 from the SoC domain send interrupts to AON cluster. These interfaces could be repurposed as Debug UART in closed system debug; interrupts from these UART instances are routed to AVIC so that the Debug UART driver running in SPE (which various debug routines interact) is getting the correct interrupt. 5. Secure Interrupts Routing Secure interrupts are generally routed to LIC and subsequently handled by the TrustZone Interrupt handler. Secure Interrupt is also routed as a fault to the HSM via error loggers in the AON cluster NoC. There are cases where the secure interrupt could be overloaded with normal functional scenarios (e.g., APB slave indicates a security access violation, such as SCR, or other violations such as an address hole via SLAVE_ERR). If the secure interrupt become overloaded, the AON Fabric asserts the Secure Interrupt to be resolved by the TrustZone software.

AON Cluster Functional Description
**Figure 9.98 Interrupt Structure**
Like any other APB peripherals in AON, AVIC access and configuration spaces are accessed via MMIO path. The AVIC port of Cortex-R5 interfaces to the PL192 and enables the following functions in hardware to minimize software overhead of servicing the interrupt. 1. 2. 3. Determine from the interrupt controller which interrupt source is requesting service. Determine where the service routine for that interrupt source is loaded. Masks that interrupt source, before re-enabling processor interrupts to permit another interrupt to be taken. Interrupt connections to PL192 include: 1. Local interrupts originating from within the AON cluster are connected to PL192 interrupt inputs; these are vectored (i.e., mapped to IRQ for low interrupt latency). Four external interrupts are connected from the LIC. Each interrupt can be an aggregation of one or more interrupts. Interrupts from selective SoC peripherals like UARTs and Doorbell units. 2. 3.

AON Cluster Functional Description AON Fabric The AON cluster uses a single FlexNoC IP for routing access to DRAM via DBB and MMIO requests (via CBB to SoC peripherals and peripherals in AON).
##### 9.13.2.12.1 AON Cluster Fabric
The AON cluster fabric uses various Software entities to access various IP’s register space. The AON Cluster fabric supports: MMIO requests from various AON initiators to SoC peripherals (via CBB), and to peripherals in AON. MMIO requests from various CBB initiators to IPs in the AON cluster. AON DMA accesses to DRAM, AON TCMs, and various MMIO requests to IPs in AON and SoC domains. 1. 2. 3. AON Cluster Fabric Topology The AON cluster fabric supports the initiators mentioned below as per the protocol and data widths. Each of the below initiator is connected to an initiator node inside the cluster fabric. Initiator Protocol Data-Width Power Domain of the initiator node Comments SPE R5’s Periphery port AXIv3 32-bit AOPG SPE R5 accesses various IP’s (both in SOC and AON) register configuration space through this port AON DMA Periphery port AXIv3 32-bit AOPG AON DMA accesses various IP’s especially IO controller’s register configuration space through this port AON DMA Memory port AXIv4 64-bit AOPG AON DMA accesses memory and AON TCM through this port CBB in SOC domain AXIv4 32-bit AOPG (MV crossing from SOC to AOPG domain) Intermediate initiator on AON Cluster fabric, through which various SoC initiators can access AON IP’s register configuration space. Note that this initiator port does not have physical path to Cortex-R5 AXI Target. AON Cluster Fabric supports the targets mentioned in the below table as per the protocol and data widths. AON Cluster Functional Description Target Protocol Data-Width Power domain of the target node Comments AST1 AXIv3 64-bit AONPG AON DMA memory accesses go through this target. AST0/1 has certain security critical configuration along with address translation setup for Cortex-R5 and DMA’s memory accesses. ASTs are placed in AONPG domain to retain all such configuration for any latency critical use cases where SPE needs early access to DRAM/MC during the warm boot. All NPG-able APB targets connect to this node via a MDMM, placed in NPG domain. Target nodes connect to the Initiator nodes via a Junction Box which has the arbiter and routing logic. In addition, cluster fabric implements common firewall and error logger/notifier/collator logic. Error Generation and Logging Error Monitor Each Initiator node in the fabric contains an Error Monitor Module. This module can raise an interrupt on the following errors: SLVERR/DECODE error Power down error Firewall error Timeout error Unsupported access error Error Notifier and Interrupt The AON Cluster fabric implements one Error Notifier module which collates interrupts from various Error Monitor blocks in the initiator nodes and generates a single interrupt signal. This

AON Cluster Functional Description interrupt is routed to both LIC and SPE-AVIC. In addition, this interrupt is routed as a fault directly to the HSM. Error Collator The AON cluster fabric implements error collators in each partition where the AON Fabric logic exists. Faults from the diagnostics implemented in the fabric logic sitting in each partition are routed to the respective error collators. In AON, since the fabric logic is implemented in both AOPG and AONPG partitions, four faults from AON fabric are routed to HSM (two from each EC i.e., a corrected and uncorrected fault from each error collator).
##### 9.13.2.12.2 Always-On Power Manager (AO-PM or PM)
The block called AO-PM contains registers and state machines which enable the Cortex-R5 and other resources to enter low power states when the Cortex-R5 is idle. Additionally, AO-PM also contains some general configuration registers related to the cluster. The AO-PM unit implements the SPE Power States and coordinates with PMC and AO-CAR to manage the SPE and System Power State transitions. It provides a programming interface to the SPE to manage the cluster's power states. The functionalities of this module include the following: 1. SPE Power State Control: Making power state transition decisions according to enabled power state configurations and triggering entry-exit sequences to/from SPE power states. SPE Power State exit management: Monitoring and responding to the processor complex and DMA engine's activity requests and wake events that trigger SPE Power State exits. Clock source management: Sending control signals to AO CAR state machines for controlling the AO PLL, switching clock sources for the processor complex for the target SPE power state. Power-gating: Handshake with PMC to support retention mode for the processor caches, TCMs RAMs, and the power gate-able portions of the AO cluster. Handshakes with NOC-PM to make sure there are no pending transactions before power gating AOPG partition and ensures NOC is ready to accept transactions post PG reset deassertion. Power Security: Supports a secure configuration of the mapping of the clocking and power resources per AO power state. PMC handshake: Handshake with PMC to support interaction of SPE power states with SC7. RTC Alarm: Implements an alarm for the SPE to be woken up from Dormant state when the timers are power-gated. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. 7. This module is not directly responsible for the SoC power states which are controlled by PMC.
##### 9.13.2.12.3 Use Cases for the AO-PM
1. 2. 3. Cortex-R5 and TCM Idle based power management Dynamic Clock Gating of TCM clocks Dynamic Power Gating of Cortex-R5 cluster, if supported

AON Cluster Functional Description 4. 5. 6. 7. Cortex-R5 Clock burst policy (For AON_CPU_NIC_CLK and AON_APB_CLK) on interrupts SRAM low power mode controls Baseline support for SC7 Boot support
##### 9.13.2.12.4 SPE Power State Management
At the core of the AO-PM Module is a Power State Transition FSM that controls transitions from SPE ACTIVE to any of the "target" low power states. These states can be SPE_IDLE, SPE_STANDBY, or SPE_DORMANT, either Shallow or Deep. Before the SPE executes WFI/WFE, it programs the power configuration registers in AO-PM to a target state, such that whenever the AO-PM detects WFI/WFE along with nCLKSTOPPED, it can readily transition to one of the targeted states. Primarily, two sets of registers must be programmed: 1. 2. TGT_PWR_STATE register (Programmed by SPE-FW). POWER_CFG_MASK registers (Set up by Power Security software). This set overrides the TGT_PWR_STATE registers. Entry into any of the low-power states is possible by two conditions: 1. Functional Trigger from the Cortex-R5: Either nWFIPIPESTOPPED or nWFEPIPESTOPPED is asserted, along with nCLKSTOPPED asserted. Debug trigger: A debug register (DBG_FEATURES_0_FORCE_START) write can also trigger a specific state machine. This is provided for ASIC debug purposes only. 2. AOPM does not enter into the low power states if the global clock override is set. Exit conditions from low power states are: !WFI/WFE/nCLKSTOPPED DMA active (Wake on a transaction on AXI-S port of the Cortex-R5) IRQ or FIQ LP_EXIT trigger (register write) DEBUG TIMEOUT (if stuck in a state longer than timer value) RTC alarm Wake Interrupt (Tier 0) SC7 wake request goes high from PMC (For Tier 1 or Tier 2 wake events) Some interrupts generated from the Cortex-R5-clusters are not routed to the local VIC but go to the LIC. These are not capable of automatically causing the PM to exit an LP state. The low power

AON Cluster Functional Description states lower the cluster clock frequencies and potentially slow down the interrupt service routine running on the external target processor. Such interrupts and their effects are analyzed below. 1. Watchdog_remote interrupt – This is the WDT 3rd expiry interrupt from the local TKE's WDT. The handler for the remote WDT wakes up the PM by issuing a software triggered exit through the LP_EXIT register. For AON, when the expiry occurs in SC7, the 3rd expiry of SPE- WDT causes an SC7 exit. This results in the AOPM coming out to an ACTIVE state and then re-entering a SHALLOW state. In the SHALLOW state, the handler for the WDT accesses the LP_EXIT register and causes a wake to ACTIVE. In order to prevent the PM from going back to a low power state, the WFI is masked by the handler inside the PM. In general, the 1st or 2nd expiry of the WDT causes an exit from the LP state – hence the 3rd expiry is not expected to occur in an LP state. However, if the 3rd expiry occurs in an LP state (or if the 1st and 2nd expiries are masked) then the handler uses the knobs described above to force the PM to exit to the low power state. HSP_SI_[1|2|3|4] interrupts – An outbound full interrupt is raised when the local processor posts a message to another processor. The local processor may execute WFI after posting the message. The PM does not need to stay in the ACTIVE state. When the target processor consumes the interrupt and clears it, the local processor does not need to move to the ACTIVE state. If the target processor requires further communication with the local processor, it posts another message that causes the HSP_SI_0 interrupt to assert and wake the PM from the ACTIVE state. An outbound empty interrupt is raised when the target processor consumes the message. The interrupt requires the target processor, not the local processor, to wake to the ACTIVE state. APB bridge error and security interrupts – The effect of these interrupts not causing an LP (Low Power) state exit is to slow down the interrupt handler routine. 2. 3. SPE-IDLE Power State SPE-Idle is a group of idle states characterized by the following steady state conditions: Cortex-R5 in Standby: nWFIPIPESTOPPED or nWFEPIPESTOPPED, and nCLKSTOPPED are asserted. The states of the L1 caches, ASTs and external paths from the SPE cluster to SoC domain are subject to ULP mode. These are idle and not being used by the Cortex-R5 actively. Second level clock gating handles the SPE and TCM clocks. I/O controllers may be clock- gated by software. DMA is idle. I/O controllers in slave mode may be active and using local buffering but those in master mode are idle. Clocks can be switched to alternative sources including OSC. Switchover to 32 kHz is allowed only when ALLOW_DEEP_I bit of AOPM_POWER_CFG_MASK_0 is set and the system is in SC7 state. The I/O controller configurations and their clock controls can be in various states depending on use cases.

AON Cluster Functional Description Entry Configuration The TCM is clock gated on assertion of nCLKSTOPPED signal. AO-PM detects this signal to gate and ungate the TCM clocks. The AO PLL may be configured by SPE-FW to be placed in a low power mode like DISABLE/ IDDQ if the I/O controllers are under S-managed clock-gated state or if their clocks are configured to be supplied from non-PLL sources like OSC and 32 kHz. When AO PLL is placed in a low power mode, the default clock source is switched to OSC. The switching of the clock source is handled by AO-CAR. AON Rail retention is not enabled in this state. The TCM does not expect to be in retention mode in this shallower idle state. BPMP and PMC control whether clocks can be switched to 32 kHz in this state when the system is in SC7. SPE-Standby Power State The SPE-Standby state is entered when the SPE subsystem has been resident in the SPE-Idle state for a programmable interval of time. SPE-Standby is similar to SPE-Idle except that the TCM and cache SRAMs are placed in a low power mode (RET). The TCMs or the caches cannot be accessed when placed in RET mode. When the RAMs are placed in RET mode, the AO rail can be externally lowered to the level of SRAM retention voltage (expected to be higher than minimum functional logic voltage) TCM and Cache RAMs are put in RET mode by the AOPM Standby sequencer when the RAM_RET bit in the AOPM_TGT_PWR_STATE_0 register is set. Other cluster RAMs are placed in RET mode under software control. Clocks and AO PLL are configured the same way as for SPE-Idle. Before the TCM is placed in retention, access to the TCM controller are blocked by the AO-PM hardware. The AO-PM also resolves race conditions between entering this low power state and an exit trigger like an interrupt showing up during entry. The L1 caches can be placed in retention mode along with the TCMs. The interrupts to the Cortex-R5 are explicitly blocked when caches are placed in retention. Accesses through the AXI-S slave port are blocked by AO-PM hardware too. Exit conditions for this state are identical to SPE-Idle state. The Deep Standby state entry is allowed only if the system is in the SC7 state and the ALLOW_DEEP_S bit in the AOPM_POWER_CFG_MASK_0 register is set. SPE-Dormant Power State The SPE wakes up on a CAN wake event to process the CAN message. The hardware architecture supports a generic partially power-gated state for the AO cluster that can also be entered more aggressively when the sensor functions are enabled in the ULP mode. This power state may also trivially be engaged when sensor functions are statically disabled in the system by configuration or by user intervention. TCMs, Caches and other RAMs in AOPG cluster can be placed in RET mode. SPE’s reset vector must point to the TCM when the processor is taken out of power-gating since the SoC domain is

AON Cluster Functional Description powered off during this time. When all the SRAMs in the VDD_RTC power domain are placed in RET mode, the VDD_RTC rail can be lowered to SRAM_VRET. AOPG cluster can be power gated completely. In addition to the low power states of the resources supported in SPE-Idle and SPE-Standby state, the OSC pad can be turned off in this state if the system is in SC7. This requires all clocks to be switched to 32 kHz either in software or in hardware or gated off prior to OSC is turned off. AOPM can enter its Deep Dormant state, only when SoC is in the SC7 state. The PM handshakes with the SC7 FSM in the PMC to ensure that the SoC is in SC7 before the PM enters the deep dormant state. There is a software knob to bypass the second clock switch (the one that switches to 32K and turns off OSC). If the BYPASS_TWO_STEP bit is set, DEEP_DORMANT is entered after PG. (There is no retention wait counter for dormant state.) The RAM_RET and RAIL_RET options are as discussed in the STBY section. The only difference is that even if no RAM_RET is requested, hardware will do RAM_RET, but it will still not override what software has requested. Exit from the SPE-Dormant state is triggered by interrupts (in the shallow state) from sources that are not power-gated and by wake events from sources that are power-gated, including the SC7 Tier 0 wake events. Thus, exit from the SPE-Dormant is automatically included in the SC7 exit sequence. Exit Handling Due to SC7 Exit When AOPM FSMs are in any non-active state, an SC7 exit of the PMC results in an exit condition of AOPM FSMs, and this exit in non-maskable. That is, unlike for other exit causes who have a mask/unmask bit in POWER_CFG_MASK register, the SC7 exit from the PMC results in AOPM exiting from LP states. While an SC7 entry of the PMC gates the entry into deep states only, an SC7 exit causes an exit whether AOPM FSMs are in their shallow or deep flavors. An SC7 exit also gates off further deep state re-entry, unless explicitly reprogrammed to do so by the BPMP before the next SC7 entry. Example: If in a deep state and an SC7 exit happens in the PMC: Some deep state -> (SC7 wake) -> Shallow state -> Transitions for exit -> Active -> (LP condition) -> Go up to Shallow only If in a shallow state and an SC7 exit happens in the PMC: Some shallow state -> (SC7 wake) -> Transition for exit -> Active -> (LP condition) -> go up to Shallow only Clock Burst on Interrupt The processor may be busy executing very low horsepower tasks but not be able to suspend all tasks and execute a WFI instruction. The processor may switch its clocks to a slow source like OSC clock. This slow clock affects the latency to a subsequent interrupt. The added latency of

AON Cluster Functional Description processing the interrupt signal sequence and the ISR at a slow clock prevents the processor from switching to the slow clock when it is not completely idle but very lazy. AOPM supports switching the processor subsystem clocks to a faster source automatically when an interrupt is triggered. The interrupt specific clock source is used in both active and low power idle states of the processor complex. When the processor is active, the SPE-FW requests the AO-PM to switch aon_cpu_clk, aon_nic_clk and aon_apb_clk to pre-programmed values in the AO-CAR. SPE-FW writes to AOPM_PWR_STATE register STATE = ACTIVE_IRQFIQ to raise this request. AO-PM sends a request to AO-CAR using the TGT_ACTIVE_IRQFIQ command index, waits for the AO-CAR to switch the clocks and acknowledge, after which it updates AOPM_PWR_STATUS to STATE = ACTIVE_IRQFIQ to reflect that the software request is completed. SPE-FW switches the clocks back to the TGT_ACTIVE state after servicing the pending interrupts. When SPE-FW switches the clocks back to TGT_ACTIVE state, the AOPM_PWR_STATUS gets updated to STATE = ACTIVE. When the processor is idle and the AO-PM has placed the subsystem in one of the low power states described above, if the exit condition is an interrupt, the AO-PM hardware requests the AOCAR to auto-switch to the faster clock sources if BURST mode is enabled. This feature leverages the index-based request/acknowledge protocol between AOPM and the AO- CAR block. BURST_CLK_EN field in AOPM_BURST_CLK_0 register must be set to enable this feature in ACTIVE state and BURST_LP_EN field of the same register must be set to enable this feature in non-ACTIVE or low power states. If the interrupt to Cortex-R5 is masked inside the PM module using the LP_EXIT_MASK register, then clock bursting is bypassed by the PM hardware upon a wake from nCLKSTOPPED or nWFIPIPESTOPPED de-assertion event.
##### 9.13.2.12.5 AO I/O DPD
AO-PM does not control any DPD control of the AO I/O pads. This is handled inside the PMC.
##### 9.13.2.12.6 SRAM Low Power Mode Management
AO-PM implements a handshake with the PMC in the Standby/Dormant states in order to put the following RAMs in retention mode. This interface constitutes a request from the AO-PM and an acknowledgement coming from the PMC. For the RAMs to be put in retention, the request line is asserted HIGH and low indicates removal of Retention mode. In the case of NO_ACK from PMC, PM FSM times out and an interrupt can be raised on NO_RET_ACK. The following RAMs are controlled by PMC: 1. 2. B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank0 B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank1

AON Cluster Functional Description 3. 4. 5. 6. 7. 8. 9. B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank2 B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank3 B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank4 B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank5 B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank6 B0TCM and B1TCM_Bank7 Cache0 LCache0 DCache0 10. 11. CAN0 CAN1 In addition to the hardware handshake, shutdown and retention controls of these Cluster RAMs can be directly controlled by software and those registers lie in the PMC module. Note: CAN RAMs are not controlled by AO-PM hardware sequencer. It is mandatory for SPE-SW to put CAN RAMs in low power mode (RET or SLEEP) if AO-PM is configured to enter the deep- dormant state, as it is illegal to have RAM in functional mode and Logic in a PG-ed state. If RAM_RET == RAIL_RET == 0, then Standby FSM becomes identical to Idle FSM, barring the fact that different CAR target request ids are sent from PM to CAR.
#### 9.13.2.13 AXI Block Support
AOPM provides support via configuration registers to block AXI requests. The following register in AO-PM supports this. Register: AOPM_AON_BLOCK_0 Fields: AOPM_AON_BLOCK_0_AON2SNIC_REQ: This bit blocks AXI requests on the control fabric to the SOC. Since AON can be operating when SOC is not powered on, it is used to block the requests going towards SOC. AOPM_AON_BLOCK_0_AON2MC_REQ: This bit in AO-PM blocks AXI requests to MC. Since AON can be operating when MC is not powered on, it is used to stop the requests going towards SOC. Additionally, there is a status register to read back status from the AXIBLOCK FSM via a block status [31:0] sideband input to AO-PM.

AON Cluster Functional Description
#### 9.13.2.14 Interrupts
AO-PM has three interrupts going out. Table 9.99 PM Interrupts Interrupt Sources Pm2vic_intr RTC_ALARM NO_CAR_ACK NO_OSC_ACK NO_RET_ACK NO_NOC_IDLE_ACK NO_NOC_IDLE Pm2lic_intr RTC_ALARM NO_CAR_ACK NO_OSC_ACK NO_RET_ACK NO_NOC_IDLE_ACK NO_NOC_IDLE Pm_actmon_intr PM Unit Actmon RTC_ALARM = When the RTC second/millisecond time matches the programmed value in the configuration registers, it generates an RTC alarm. The RTC generates an interrupt or generate an exit from low power states. The interrupt handler for the RTA Alarm Wake reprograms the AOPM_RTC_ALARM_TIMER and/or AOPM_RTC_ALARM_MSEC_TIMER registers before clearing the interrupt so that the interrupt does not fire spuriously. BPMP_PM (bpmp_pm2lic_int) and BPMP- PM (bpmp_pm2vic_int) are generated from the same sources, but have a different set of status (pre-mask), Mask, Set, and Clear registers for VIC and for LIC interrupts. Note that SPE should not be interrupted for NO_DVS_ACK. The interrupt to NO_DVS_ACK can be selectively masked off for SPE but enabled for LIC (for BPMP). NO_CAR_ACK = When CAR is requested to change the clock source or assert/de-assert PG resets, but the PM FSM times out waiting for an ACK, this interrupt is raised. The PM FSM cannot assume a good clock or a complete reset sequence, and the BPMP may need to come in and reset the PM and the system to a known good state of clocks. NO_OSC_ACK = When PMC has been requested to turn on/off the OSC ACK is obtained, instead the PM FSM times out waiting for an ACK from the PMC. NO_RET_ACK = When PMC has been requested to put RAMs in/out retention mode, but the PM does not get an ACK, the PM FSM times out waiting for an ACK from the PMC. In this case, PM FSM cannot assume any good state of cluster RAMs (partial sequencing of RAM low power mode is also a possible scenario). Upon narrowing down that the interrupt is due to NO_RET_ACK, software

AON Cluster Functional Description can check the corresponding RAM status bits and also the PG controller status register to infer if there is a hang in the PG controller in the PMC. NO_NOC_IDLE_ACK = When NOC_PM has been requested to query power disconnect modules/T- NIUs that there are no pending transactions. If the PM does not get an ACK, the PM FSM timer times out. NO_NOC_IDLE = When NOC_PM does not give an IDLE indication for the PM dormant state machine to move forward, the PM FSM times out.
#### 9.13.2.15 Cortex-R5 Activity Monitor
The AO-PM has a unit ACTMON. The interrupt from the unit ACTMON is not merged with the PM interrupt. It is separately routed to the local VIC and to LIC. The PM uses this ACTMON to detect idle periods of the processor complex and monitors key events that the Cortex-R5 exposes on its event bus. The idle state of the Cortex-R5 is not exposed to the event bus. Therefore, the idle signals nCLKSTOPPED, nWFIPIPESTOPPED, and nWFEPIPESTOPPED must be separately exported to detect idle period statistics and use the information for scaling the performance of the Cortex- R5.

AON Cluster Functional Description
**Figure 9.99 Cortex-R5 Unit ACTMON**
Outputs from the Cortex-R5 are sampled at the processor clock frequency and a cumulative counter incremented for every cycle that the unit_active signal is asserted. The cumulative count is compared with a target count. When the cumulative count in processor clock rate reaches the target value, the ACTMON is notified. The EVENTBUS signals hooked up to the ACTMON are indicative of the following events. EVENTBUS[5]: Indicates that the instruction is architecturally executed. Asserted on every cycle when an instruction was architecturally executed by the processor. EVENTBUS[16]: Stalls because instruction buffer cannot deliver an instruction. This can indicate an instruction cache miss. Asserted every cycle where the condition is present.

AON Cluster Functional Description EVENTBUS[19]: External memory request. Examples of this are cache refill, non-cacheable accesses, write-through writes, cache line evictions (write-back). EVENTBUS[20]: Stalls because of Load Store Unit (LSU) being busy. The event takes place each clock cycle where the condition is met. A high incidence of this event indicates the pipeline is often waiting for transactions to complete on the external bus.
#### 9.13.2.16 Programming Model
##### 9.13.2.16.1 AOPM Address Map
This address space is address decoded within PM into PM_IMPL (the functional PM part), the PM_ACTMON (of the unit ACTMON), and the rest is reserved. ##### 9.13.2.16.2 AON Power States Programming Guidelines
SPE- IDLE Entry Sequence Agent Step Cortex-R5 SW Set up AO-PM with power state transition command by writing to AOPM_TGT_PWR _STATE register. STATE == IDLE TCM_ACTIVE (implicit for IDLE mode) Set up AO-CAR with power state transition info by writing to registers described in the Clocks Chapter to set up the clock source to switch to and the power state of the AOPLL. It could be either of these registers: TGT_IDLE_SHALLOW TGT_IDLE_DEEP Cortex-R5 SW Execute WFI.

AON Cluster Functional Description Agent Step Clock gating Logic All second level clock gating controls kick in at this stage except the TCM clocks, backbone clocks for DMA, NOC branches that may be actively used by the DMA during this time along with any active I/O clock(s). Software may additionally FLCG I/O clock sources or switch these to OSC or 32K. Software accordingly programs TGT_IDLE before executing WFI so that AO-PM or AO-CAR hardware does not turn the PLL off when any of the I/O controllers are actively using these clock sources. AO-DMA DMA goes idle and gets clock gated at the second level. AXI-S AXI-S port goes idle as DMA and I/O controllers go idle. Cortex-R5 AO-PM Engage the second level clock gates on TCM clocks. AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to a slower clock. AO-CAR Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to TGT_IDLE_SHALLOW sources if enabled. Place AO-PLL in TGT_IDLE_SHALLOW mode. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register. Set CURRENT_STATE == IDLE_SHALLOW and other fields as per entry sequence. AO-PM Check for AOPM_POWER_CFG_MASK_TGT_DEEP_IDLE. If not DISABLE-d, enter DEEP_IDLE state. AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 clocks to TGT_IDLE_DEEP. Place AO-PLL in low power TGT_IDLE_DEEP mode. AO-CAR Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to TGT_IDLE_SOURCE if enabled. Place AO-PLL in TGT_IDLE mode. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register. Set CURRENT_STATE == IDLE_DEEP. Other fields as per entry sequence. SPE-IDLE Exit Sequence Once an exit condition is triggered: Agent Step Cortex- R5 Detects interrupt from AVIC or detects request on AXI-S port to come out of Standby mode AO-PM Release TCM clock gates within three cycles of nCLKSTOPPED getting deasserted. Detect exit from the SPE-Idle state and capture the cause for wake up in a status register. If the wake up is due to an SC7 wake event: 1. 2. Re-enable the DEEP_IDLE override in hardware. Optionally raise an interrupt to SPE. AO-PM Take AOPLL out of low-power mode. Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks back to the mode in which the clocks were running prior to entering this SPE-Idle state.

AON Cluster Functional Description Agent Step AO-CAR Place AOPLL in TGT_ACTIVE or TGT_ACTIVE_IRQFIQ mode. Switch Cortex-R5 clocks to TGT_ACTIVE or TGT_ACTIVE_IRFIQ source. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register. Set CURRENT_STATE == ACTIVE or ACTIVE_IRQFIQ. SPE-STANDBY Entry Sequence Agent Step Cortex- R5 SW Set up AO-PM with power state transition command by writing to: AOPM_TGT_PWR _STATE register. STATE == STANDBY RAM_RET or RAIL_RET enabled. RAM_RET = RAM ret mode RAIL_RET = AON rail retention Set RAM_RET and/or RAIL_RET. Set up AO-CAR with power state transition info for clock sources and AOPLL. TGT_STBY_SHALLOW TGT_STBY_DEEP Cortex- R5 SW Execute WFI. Cortex- R5 HW AXI-S port goes idle AO-PM Execute the entry steps for entering SPE-Idle. During these steps, AO-PM requests AO-CAR to use TGT_STBY_SHALLOW commands. SPE-Standby entry is stepped through SPE-Idle. Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register. CURRENT_STATE = STBY_SHALLOW_IDLE Optionally, use the DMA_ACTIVE (MC-side) indicator from the SPE-DMA to infer idleness. AO-PM Block TCM accesses from AXI-S port upon expiry of the retention entry delay timer. AO-PM Block interrupts from reaching the Cortex-R5 from VIC. AO-PM Check if RAM_RET is enabled. Handshakes with PMC. PMC Completes RAM retention sequencing and ACKs back to PM. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register with STATE == STBY_SHALLOW. AO-PM Check for AOPM_POWER_CFG_MASK_TGT_DEEP_STANDBY. If DISABLE-d, enter DEEP_STANDBY state. AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 clocks to TGT_STBY source. Place AO-PLL in low power mode TGT_STBY. AO-CAR Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to TGT_STBY if enabled. Switch non Cortex-R5 clocks to OSC if they are sourced from AO-PLL. Place AO-PLL in TGT_STBY mode. Acknowledge AO-PM.

AON Cluster Functional Description Agent Step AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register. Set CURRENT_STATE == STANDBY_DEEP. Other fields as per entry sequence. SPE-STANDBY Exit Sequence Agent Step Cortex- R5 Detects interrupt from AVIC or detects request on AXI-S port to come out of Standby mode. AO-PM Release TCM clock gates within three cycles of nCLKSTOPPED getting deasserted. Detect exit from SPE-Standby state and capture the cause for wake-up in a status register. If the exit condition is due to an SC7 wake request from PMC 1. 2. Re-enable DEEP_STANDBY override in hardware. Optionally raise an interrupt to SPE. Before taking the rail out of retention, aon_cpu_clk, aon_nic_clk and aon_apb_clk clocks should be switched back to at least the OSC clock if they were running off 32 kHz. This is to not incur extra latency on the exit path by operating the logic that controls rail voltage at a very slow clock. AO-PM Switch aon_cpu_clk, aon_nic_clk and aon_apb_clk back to OSC and wait for acknowledgement from AO-CAR. AO-CAR Switch AOPLL and Cortex-R5 clocks to TGT_STBY_SHALLOW. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Handshake with PMC to take TCMs and caches out of retention mode PMC Brings RAMs out of retention modes AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 clocks and AOPLL back to their ACTIVE state sources. This step must wait for RAIL_RET exit to complete. AO-PM implements the rail retention exit timer. AO-CAR Switch Cortex-R5 clocks and AOPLL to TGT_ACTIVE or TGT_ACTIVE_IRQFIQ mode. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Upon completion of RAIL_RET exit, RAM_RET exit requests, unblock TCM accesses on AXI-S path and unblock interrupts. Do not wait for clocks and AOPLL to switch to TGT_ACTIVE mode. AO-PM Upon completion of RAIL_RET exit, RAM_RET exit requests, unblock interrupt. Do not wait for clocks and AOPLL to switch to TGT_ACTIVE mode. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register Set CURRENT_STATE == ACTIVE or ACTIVE_IRQFIQ. SPE-DORMANT Entry Sequence

AON Cluster Functional Description Agent Step Cortex-R5 SW Prepare I/O controllers for power-gating mode. For each I/O controller: 1. 2. 3. 4. Execute context save operations after the controller is in idle state. Clock gate the controller. Assert reset to the controller. Switch I/O controller clocks to 32 kHz. Put the CAN message RAMs into SLEEP mode. Flush and disable the L1 caches and place them in SLEEP mode. Cortex-R5 SW Set up AO-PM with power state transition command by writing to AOPM_TGT_PWR _STATE register. STATE == DORMANT RAM_RET and/or RAIL_RET is enabled. Set up AO-CAR with power state transition info by writing to registers described in Clocks Chapter TGT_DORMANT_SHALLOW (should be no slower than OSC) TGT_DORMANT (expected to be 32 kHz) (Can optionally set up the Rail retention Control Mode in the PMC.) Cortex-R5 SW Execute WFI Cortex-R5 AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to TGT_DORMANT_SHALLOW. Place AO-PLL in low power mode. AO-CAR Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to TGT_DORMANT_SHALLOW if enabled. Place AO-PLL in TGT_DORMANT_SHALLOW mode. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Block accesses at the AXI-S interface. This prevents TCM accesses when the TCM is in retention. Block interrupts at the output of the AVIC. This prevents Cortex-R5 from being woken up when TCM and caches are held in retention. AO-PM Put RAMs in RET mode by implementing handshake with the PMC. PMC Upon receiving request from AO-PM, the PMC PG Controller puts the AOPG RAMs in RET mode and sends an ACK to AO-PM. Before switching the AO-PM clock itself to 32 kHz, the reset and PG sequence, OSC control sequence must be completed. AO-PM first waits for the PMC to go into SC7, executes the below sequences handshaking with PMC, and then switches the clocks to 32 kHz. AO-PM Wait for PMC to indicate that SC7 entry is completed. PMC De-assert SC7 commit indication once SC7 entry is completed and there is no pending wake event detected for SC7 exit. Wait for AO-PM to deassert AOPM acknowledgement before responding to a subsequent SC7 action. The rest of the Dormant state entry sequence holds off SC7 wake events. AO-PM Hold off PMC from exiting SC7. AOPM AO-PM sends a request to NOC PM to ensure there are no outstanding transactions in NoC. AON-NOC Handshakes with T-NIUs in NOC to ensure no outstanding transactions, and sends an ack back to the PM. AON-NOC Handshakes with power disconnect modules in NoC and sends a second ACK to the PM.

AON Cluster Functional Description Agent Step AO-PM Once idle is received from NoC, PM sequences the module resets and module clock enables in preparation for power-gating AOPG domain. The modules that are reset in Hardware are Cortex-R5 resets (nSYSPORESET, PRESETDBG, DBGRESET and nRESET) AON VIC reset AON Fabric resets 1. 2. 3. The module that can be reset only when the system is in SC7 is the AON-NoC resets 1. The AO-PM waits for the PMC to go into SC7 before resetting any module for power-gating. AO-CAR Assert requested resets and gate requested clocks and acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Place the Cortex-R5 in HALT mode until the PG exit sequence is completed AO-PM Trigger PG state machine to assert clamp enables and sleep enables for AOPG domain. Wait for completion of PG entry sequence. AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to a clock source programmed in TGT_DORMANT_DEEP_CLKSRC and assert AOPLL low power mode. AO-CAR Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks to TGT_DORMANT_CLKSRC if enabled and place AOPLL in low power mode defined by this configuration. Acknowledge AO-PM. AO-PM Request PMC to turn OSC off. PMC Conditionally turn OSC off if enabled by BPMP. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register CURRENT_STATE == DORMANT_DEEP SPE-DORMANT Exit Sequence Agent Step AO-PM Detects exit conditions: Pending interrupt (in shallow state) from AVIC outputs Pending wake events from the Wake Engine SC7 indication to exit low power states Software triggered exit from external NoC master access (valid only until AOPG is power gated) 1. 2. 3. 4. AO-PM Request for OSC pad to be turned on PMC Turn OSC pad on AO-PM Switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks back to TGT_DORMANT_SHALLOW (required to be OSC). This also switches AOPLL to the corresponding mode. AO-PM Requests PMC PG state machine to get RAMs out of RET mode and AOPG domain out of power gating. If the exit condition is due to an SC7 wake request from PMC, then re-enable DEEP_DORMANT override in hardware.

AON Cluster Functional Description Agent Step AO-PM Once AOPG domain is unpower gated, take the modules out of reset that are not under software reset control. This sends a request to the NOC to do power-ungating steps. Then indicates to the SC7 sequencer that AON exit actions are complete. Once the rail is exited from retention voltage, take the TCMs and SRAMs out of RET mode. Switch AOPLL back to TGT_ACTIVE and switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks back to TGT_ACTIVE sources. Wait for ACK from AO-CAR. Request CAR to deassert resets to all hardware-controlled modules. The modules whose resets are removed in hardware are: 1. 2. 3. Cortex-R5 resets (nSYSPORESET, PRESETDBG, DBGRESET and nRESET) AON VIC reset AON Fabric resets AO-CAR Switch AOPLL back to TGT_ACTIVE and switch Cortex-R5 subsystem clocks back to TGT_ACTIVE sources. Switch PWR-I2C clock back to TGT_ACTIVE source. Send acknowledgement to AO-PM. Take modules out of reset as requested by AO-PM and send acknowledgement back to AO-PM. AO-PM Once TCMs are out of RET mode, unblock the AXI-S. AO-PM Once the Cortex-R5 resets are removed and AO-CAR sends an acknowledgement back, and the SRAMs have also been taken out of retention mode, take the Cortex-R5 out of HALT mode. AO-PM Update AOPM_PWR_STATUS register CURRENT_STATE == ACTIVE
##### 9.13.2.16.3 AO-CAR
The block called AO-CAR is the CAR parts that reside in the AO voltage domain. AO-CAR provides the clocks and resets to both the AON cluster and the other blocks that are inside the AO voltage domain.AO-CAR
##### 9.13.2.16.4 DMA Controller
The AON cluster DMA controller is an eight-channel implementation of the central DMA controller. The DMA request from the AON Cluster (I2C[2:0], SPI, UART, and DMIC) are connected to the local DMA controller. Refer to the General Purpose DMA (GPC-DMA, AON, BPMP, and SCE DMA) chapter in this TRM for more details. Table 9.100 DMA Request Mapping Block TX DMA Request Port (DMA_TX [31:0]) RX DMA Request Port (DMA_RX [31:0]) Reserved I2C2 (AON_I2C2) I2C8 (AON_I2C3) SPI2 (AON_SPI1)

AON Cluster Functional Description Block TX DMA Request Port (DMA_TX [31:0]) RX DMA Request Port (DMA_RX [31:0]) UARTC (AON UARTC) UARTJ (SBSA_UART) DMIC N/A GTE N/A UART6 [from SoC for closed system debug] UART8 [from SoC for closed system debug]
##### 9.13.2.16.5 Address Translation
The AON Cluster is required to support sending requests to DRAM that indicate to the SMMU if the request requires translation to support a physical carve-out. The SMMU needs to handle requests differently based on if a translation is requested. Since the Cortex-R5 is not capable of indicating if a request requires translation, an Address Space Translation Engine (AST) is used to define the address regions that require translation. The AST is also used to remap the Cortex-R5 and DMA generated address to prevent address space collision for I/O virtual addresses. The AON cluster includes two eight region AST modules. Refer to Address Space Translation (AST) for more information. The AON Cluster is only allowed to bypass SMMU translation when accessing the AON Cluster-only carve-out. If a translation is not requested, the SMMU must bypass the address translation and ensure the address is inside the AON Cluster DRAM region. If a translation is requested, the SMMU performs the translation and ensures that the translated address is not in the AON Cluster region (or any other protected region).
##### 9.13.2.16.6 Shared Mailboxes
The AON cluster uses shared MMIO mailbox registers to communicate between the Cortex-R5 other processors in the system. The mailbox implementation is defined in the Hardware Synchronization Primitives (HSP) chapter of this TRM. The HSP in the AON cluster uses the following configuration i.e., eight Shared Mail Box Instances (nSM) and four Shared Semaphore (nSS) instances. The number of Shared interrupts i.e., nSI is five. nSM nAS nSS nDB nSI Notes SI[0] is sent to the AVIC. [SI[4:1] are sent to the LIC.

AON Cluster Functional Description
##### 9.13.2.16.7 Timekeeping Engine (TKE)
Cortex-R5 does not have built-in timers, the timers are integrated into the BPMP subsystem with an external Timekeeping Engine (TKE). The timekeeping unit provides the following functionalities: 1. 2. 3. Timers (NV_timers) Watchdog (WDT) Timestamp counter (TSC) read-back Table 9.101 AON TKE Configuration Parameter Value Number of NV_timers (nT) Number of watchdogs (nW) Interrupt routing Disabled Number of shared interrupts exposed TSC input type (isSerial) 1 (Serial)
**Figure 9.100 AON Timers and WDT Hookup**

AON Cluster Functional Description Watchdog Timer A watchdog timer associated with the AON Cortex-R5 is instanced to monitor Cortex-R5 CPU's health. The watchdog timer has robust restart mechanisms like windowed watchdog and Question and Answer watchdog. AON cluster has a dedicated watchdog timer instanced in the cluster. This enables us to architect the functionality of this timer as per AON clusters specific requirements.
##### 9.13.2.16.8 Timestamping (GTE)
The AON cluster implements a timestamp module (GTE) for logging the current TSC value when interrupts or GPIO events occur.
##### 9.13.2.16.9 GTE and DMA
The AON DMA engine can be used to read from the GTE timestamp FIFO instead of reading the FIFO using the Cortex-R5. One use case is for the GTE to timestamp the GPIO changes to recover a waveform (for example handling IR receive). To use GTE and DMA in this manner, the following configuration must be used. GTE: GTE_GPIO_TECTRL_0[AUTOADVADDR] = 0x3 GTE_GPIO_TECTRL_0[OCCUPANCYTHRESHOLD] = 0x1 GTE_GPIO_TECTRL_0[INTERRUPTENABLE] = 0x1 DMA: GPCDMA_FLV_8CH_NON_SAFE_CHANNEL_CH<X>_MMIO_SEQ_0[MMIO_BURST] = 0x7 GPCDMA_FLV_8CH_NON_SAFE_CHANNEL_CH<X>_MMIO_SEQ_0[MMIO_ADDR_WRAP] = 0x4 GPCDMA_FLV_8CH_NON_SAFE_CHANNEL_CH<X>_SRC_PTR_0[SRC_PTR] = GTE base address GPCDMA_FLV_8CH_NON_SAFE_CHANNEL_CH<X>_MC_SEQ_0[MC_BURST] = 0x0 GPCDMA_FLV_8CH_NON_SAFE_CHANNEL_CH<X>_DMA_BYTE_TRA_0[TRANSFER_COUNT] = 8x4x (number of samples) When using this configuration, the GTE interrupt in the AVIC must be masked.
##### 9.13.2.16.10 I2C
The AON cluster implements two I2C controllers.

AON Cluster Functional Description Table 9.102 AON I2C Controllers Global AMAP Name Key Usage Examples I2C2 Camera configuration, Touch control, Sensor interfaces I2C8 Display Aggregator, Sensor Hub Control
##### 9.13.2.16.11 SPI
The AON cluster implements one SPI controller. Table 9.103 AON SPI Controller AON SPI Instance Global AMAP Name AON_SPI SPI2
##### 9.13.2.16.12 UART
The AON cluster implements two UARTs for primary debug purposes. UARTC is an instance of the standard UART IP, but is implemented as a two pin UART with the CTS and RTS pins tied off so the IP can always send and receive data. UARTJ is the SBSA Compliant UART for debug purposes. See Universal Asynchronous Receiver/Transmitter (UART) Table 9.104 AON UARTs Global AMAP Name UART Type Usage Details UARTC 2pin Primary Two Pin Debug UART. Can also be controlled by BPMP and CCPLEX with interrupts routed to BPMP cluster and LIC. This is the case for flow control signals also, i.e., routed to BPMP Cluster DMA and GPC DMA. UART_J 2 pin SBSA Compliant UART.
##### 9.13.2.16.13 PWM
The AON cluster implements one PWM. The details of the PMW can be found in the Pulse Width Modulator (PWM) chapter of this document.
##### 9.13.2.16.14 GPIO Controllers
The AON cluster implements a GPIO controller and pinmux module. Both modules have separate APB interfaces. There are four interrupts (two functional and two time-stamp interrupts) from the GPIO controller. One functional interrupt and one timestamp interrupt is sent from the GPIO block to the AON interrupt controller. All functional and timestamp interrupts is sent to LIC.

AON Programming Guidelines
##### 9.13.2.16.15 DMIC
The AON cluster implements a DMIC controller for supporting voice wake functionality. The AON DMIC controller is optimized for low power voice wake requirements.
##### 9.13.2.16.16 CEC
The Consumer Electronic Controller (CEC) unit is added in the AO domain. The motivation for adding the controller to AON is to be able to wake the system up from SC7 only on messages indicated to the SoC and not to wake up on unintended or spurious toggles of the input (wake capable pad).
### 9.13.3 AON Programming Guidelines
#### 9.13.3.1 Power Management
##### 9.13.3.1.1 Cluster Power State Definitions
The AO Power State framework consists of SPE power states on one hand and the cluster's activity levels mapped to System Power States on the other. The SPE subsystem in the AO cluster is in one of four power states: 1. 2. 3. 4. SPE-Active SPE-Idle SPE-Standby SPE-Dormant

AON Programming Guidelines
**Figure 9.101 SPE Power States Hierarchy within System Power States Framework**
These power states are defined by the sensor processor and sensor I/Os expected activity levels. The system and power management functions in the AO cluster operate at various levels of activity but are never switched off completely except when the SoC is fully powered off (shut down). At the cluster level there is no specific idle or standby state defined. The AO cluster is an always-on domain in the chip. In any of the SoC power states, the AO cluster could be in any of its own power states. However, there are some constraints on the AO cluster state while the chip transitions into and out of the SC7 SoC states.

AON Programming Guidelines
**Figure 9.102 AO Rail Power States Transition Framework**
In the steady state, any of the AO cluster power states (except complete power-off) are supported by hardware in any of the SoC power states.
##### 9.13.3.1.2 Cortex-R5 CPU Halted (Clock Gating)
If the CPU is idle for a short period of time during WFI state, then it can be halted which results in its CPU clock-gating. The WFI instruction is executed for putting CPU into halt. After executing WFI, CPU disables most of the clocks in the CPU except the clock for the small wake up logic clock. Exit from halt state occurs when the CPU detects an interrupt on IRQ or FIQ pins.
##### 9.13.3.1.3 TCM Clock Gating
The TCM interface clock can be gated when there are no pending DMA requests and the Cortex-R5 is halted. The nCLKSTOPPED signal is used to indicate when the TCM clock can be gated. The TCM clock must be restarted in no more than four clocks after nCLKSTOPPED is deasserted.
##### 9.13.3.1.4 OSC Power Down
To reduce SC7 power when the AON Cluster is idle for an extended period (greater than 3 ms), all AON Cluster clocks except for the 32 kHz clock can be disabled by powering down the OSC pad. When the OSC is powered down, only the RTC, or an external event, can wake the AON Cluster.

AON Programming Guidelines
##### 9.13.3.1.5 Software Enable Disable of AON PLL
The AON cluster clocking logic does not allow the AON Cortex-R5 to directly turn on the AON cluster PLL. When the SoC is not in SC7, the AON Cortex-R5 can make a request to BPMP to enable or disable the PLL (normally the AON PLL is on when the SoC is on). When the SoC is in SC7, the BPMP is not powered. If the AON Cortex-R5 requires the PLL to turn on and off in SC7, the Cortex- R5 firmware must use the ACTIVE and ACTIVE_IRQFIQ power states defined in AOPM. The AON Cortex-R5 can use these two states to define a state with the PLL on (ACTIVE_IRQFIQ) and a state with the PLL off (ACTIVE). The following conditions must be met for AON firmware to control the PLL state in SC7. No I/O controllers can be configured to use a clock from the AON PLL. The BPMP must configure the ACTIVE_IRQFIQ and ACTIVE clock settings prior to entering SC7. Prior to executing WFI firmware must ensure that any previous software request is complete by a. b. [AON-R5-FW] Read AON_SW_TGT_REQ. If 1, go to Step 2, else go to Step 4. [AON-R5-FW] Poll AON_SW_TGT_ACK until it is 1 in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register. [AON-R5-FW] Program AON_SW_TGT_REQ to 0 in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register. [AON-R5-FW] Poll AON_SW_TGT_ACK in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register until it is set to 0 by hardware. c. d. ACTIVE to ACTIVE_IRQFIQ Firmware Sequence Entering the ACTIVE_IRQFIQ state typically requires an interrupt to be triggered. To prevent the PLL from being turned on every time an interrupt occurs, the ACTIVE_IRQFIQ state should be disabled: (AOPM_BURST_CLK_0[BURST_CLK_EN]= 0 and AOPM_BURST_CLK_0[BURST_LP_EN]= 0). 1. 2. [AON-R5-FW] Read AON_SW_TGT_REQ. If 1, go to Step 2, else go to Step 4. [AON-R5-FW] Poll AON_SW_TGT_ACK until it is 1 in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register. [AON-R5-FW] Program AON_SW_TGT_REQ to 0 in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register. [AON-R5-FW] Poll AON_SW_TGT_ACK in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register until it is set to 0 by hardware. [AON-R5-FW] Program the AON_SW_TGT_STATE field in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register to 0x1. 3. 4. 5.

AON Programming Guidelines 6. [AON-R5-FW] Program the AON_SW_TGT_REQ bit in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register to 1. [CAR HW] Transition to ACTIVE_IRQFIQ state and set AON_SW_TGT_ACK when complete. 7. ACTIVE_IRQFIQ to ACTIVE Sequence 1. 2. [AON-R5-FW] Read AON_SW_TGT_REQ. If 1, go to Step 2, else go to Step 4. [AON-R5-FW] Poll AON_SW_TGT_ACK until it is 1 in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register. [AON-R5-FW] Program AON_SW_TGT_REQ to 0 in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register. [AON-R5-FW] Poll AON_SW_TGT_ACK in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register until it is set to 0 by hardware. [AON-R5-FW] Program the AON_SW_TGT_STATE field in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register to 0x0. [AON-R5-FW] Program the AON_SW_TGT_REQ bit in the CLK_RST_CONTROLLER_AON_SEQ_SW_INTERFACE_CTL_0 register to 1. [CAR HW] Transition to ACTIVE state and set AON_SW_TGT_ACK when complete. 3. 4. 5. 6. 7.
##### 9.13.3.1.6 AON Cluster Power Gating
The AON cluster supports power gating most of the units within the cluster to minimize the AON power to meet the Automotive CAN standby power targets. PMC also has control register for power gating the Cortex-R5 cache RAMs, the BTCM RAMs, and the CAN controller RAMs. The figure below shows the expected PG control connections in AON.

AON Programming Guidelines
**Figure 9.103 NPG vs PG view of AON IPs**
Gating Entry Sequence 1. [AON-R5-FW] Detects an idle condition when system in SC7 that can tolerate greater than 10 ms of wake time. [AON-R5-FW] Enables wake detection on for AON external wake sources in PMC. [AON-R5-FW] Asserts Reset to each power gateable I/O controller. [AON-R5-FW] Stops first level clocks to each power gateable I/O controller. [AON-R5-FW] Save any required core logic state (Cortex-R5, AVIC, TKE, GTE, HSP) state. [AON-R5-FW] Asserts reset to TKE, GTE, HSP. [AON-R5-FW] Stops first level clocks to TKE, GTE, HSP. [AON-R5-FW] Sets the target power state to DORMANT in AO-PM. [AON-R5-FW] Executes WFI which triggers power gating for the AO cluster logic including the CAN controllers. [PMC] Waits for external wake event. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. 7. 8. 9. 10.

AON Programming Guidelines Power Gating Exit Sequence 1. 2. 3. 4. [PMC] Wake received and triggers AO-PM. [AO-PM] Restores AO Cluster to Active state. [AON-R5-FW] Enable first level clocks to TKE, GTE, HSP. [AON-R5-FW] Deasserts reset to TKE, GTE, HSP. a. b. Reset to TKE should be removed after GTE reset if GTE time stamping is used. See the Timers chapter for details on resyncing the GTE and TKE with the TSC after exiting PG. 5. 6. 7. 8. [AON-R5-FW] Restore required state to core logic. [AON-R5-FW] Enables first level clocks to each power required I/O controllers. [AON-R5-FW] Deasserts Reset to each required I/O controller. [AON-R5-FW] Initialize required I/O controllers for normal operation. Cortex-R5 Cache Power Gating When the system enters SC7, the AON Cortex-R5 can no longer access DRAM. Prior to SC7 entry the AON Cortex-R5 must flush and disable its caches. To save leakage the Cortex-R5 caches can be power-gated after the caches are disabled. Power Gating Entry Sequence 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. 7. [SW-AP] Decides to go into SC7. [SW-AP] Notifies AON Cluster firmware of SC7 Entry. [FW-AON R5] Flushes L1 data cache and write buffers. [FW-AON R5] Disables the instruction and data caches. [FW-AON R5] Programs AON Cortex-R5 Cache Power-gating control register in PMC. [HW-PMC] Power gates Cortex-R5 cache by asserting the cache SD pins. [FW-AON R5] Notifies AP/BPMP that it is safe to enter SC7. Power Gating Exit Sequence 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. [FW-BPMP] Notifies AON Cluster firmware that system is out of SC7. [FW-AON R5] Programs AON Cortex-R5 Cache Power-gating control register in PMC. [HW-PMC] Deasserts the SD pins to the Cortex-R5 cache RAMs. [FW-AON R5] Enables the instruction and data caches. [FW-AON R5] Performs invalidate all to initialize the instruction and data caches. BTCM Power Gating The BTCM for the AON Cortex-R5 can enter power gating by: 1. 2. Software initiated RAM Shutdown Hardware initiated RAM Sleep or Deep Sleep

AON Programming Guidelines 3. Software initiated RAM Sleep or Deep Sleep BTCM RAM Shutdown Software initiated RAM shutdown is controlled from PMC. PMC contains one power-gating control register for each BTCM bank. When a bank is placed in SD, the BTCM logic must return an error is the bank is accessed. Software is responsible for saving any data in the TCM bank to DRAM if state needs to be maintained. Power Gating Entry Sequence 1. 2. 3. 4. [FW-AON R5] Decides to go put TCM bank in SD [FW-AON R5] Copies any required data to DRAM. [FW-AON R5] Programs AON TCM Bank N Power-gating control register in PMC. [HW-PMC] Power gates Cortex-R5 cache by asserting the cache SD pins. Power Gating Exit Sequence 1. 2. 3. 4. [FW-AON R5] Determines a TCM Bank needs to be enabled [FW-AON R5] Programs AON TCM Bank N Power gating control register in PMC. [HW-PMC] Deasserts the SD pins to the Cortex-R5 cache RAMs [FW-AON R5] Restores TCM data from DRAM if required. CAN Power Gating The two CAN controllers are power gated at the same time the AON cluster core logic is power gated. CAN Power Gating Entry Sequence 1. [CAN-SW] Detects idle condition (involves detecting idle condition of network and controller) and system in SC7. [CAN-SW] Puts external Transceiver in Low power (or sleep or listen only) mode. [CAN-SW] Enables Wake detection on CAN WAKE (can be Rx pad for some transceivers) Pad in PMC. [CAN-SW] Asserts Reset to CAN controller. [CAN-SW] Stop CAN[1:2] first Level Clocks. [CAN-SW] Writes to the CAN[1:2] Power-gating control registers in PMC to power gate the CAN message RAM. [CAN-SW] Save any required Cortex-R5 and AVIC state. [CAN-SW] Sets the target power state to DORMANT in AO-PM. [CAN-SW] Executes WFI which triggers power gating for the AO cluster logic including the CAN controllers. [PMC] Waits for Wake event from CAN Network. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. 7. 8. 9. 10. CAN Power Gating Exit Sequence

AON Programming Guidelines 1. 2. 3. 4. [PMC] Wake received and triggers AO-PM. [AO-PM] Restores AO Cluster to Active state. [CAN-SW] Restore required state to Cortex-R5 and AVIC. [CAN-SW] Writes to the CAN[1:2] Power-gating control registers in PMC to ungate the CAN message RAM. [CAN-SW] Enable Clocks. [CAN-SW] Deassert reset. [CAN-SW] Disable Wake on CAN receive pad. [CAN-SW] Bring transceiver out of low power mode. [CAN-SW] Initialize controllers for normal operation. 5. 6. 7. 8. 9.
#### 9.13.3.2 AON Cluster SC7 Entry
Access from the AON cluster to the SOC is blocked by the software when entering SC7. If requests are in flight when the block logic is engaged it is possible a deadlock could occur. Software should follow the sequence below to ensure this deadlock does not happen. 1. 2. BPMP notifies AON FW to stop all SOC access (MMIO and DRAM) via an IPC message AON firmware performs all necessary steps to be able to operate with no SOC access. (Swap code into TCM, flush, and Disable caches, etc.) After this point AON firmware is executing only from TCM. AON firmware sends IPC to BPMP that it is safe to disable SOC access BPMP acknowledges IPC by writing to HSP mailbox in AON. AON FW detects AON mailbox write and acknowledges by writing to AON HSP. BPMP polls AON HSP waiting for the acknowledgment from AON. When the acknowledgment is received, PSC writes to AOPM to enable the block function. 3. 4. 5. 6. 7.
#### 9.13.3.3 AON Cortex-R5 Activity Monitor
The unit activity monitor is a part of the AO-PM module. The interrupt from the unit ACTMON is not merged with the AO-PM interrupt. It is separately routed to the local VIC and to LIC. AON uses a type-1 unit ACTMON [refer to the Activity Monitor (ACTMON) chapter of this document] to detect idle periods of the processor complex and monitor a few key events that the Cortex-R5 exposes on its event bus. The idle state of the Cortex-R5 is not exposed to the event bus. Therefore, the idle signals nCLKSTOPPED, nWFIPIPESTOPPED, and nWFEPIPESTOPPED must be separately exported to detect idle period statistics and use the information for scaling the performance of the Cortex-R5. The outputs from the Cortex-R5 are sampled at the processor clock frequency and a cumulative counter incremented for every cycle that the unit_active signal is asserted. The cumulative count is

AON Programming Guidelines compared with a target count. When the cumulative count in processor clock rate reaches the target value, the ACTMON is notified. The EVENTBUS signals hooked up to the ACTMON are indicative of the following events. EVENTBUS[5]: Indicates that the instruction is architecturally executed. Asserted on every cycle when an instruction was architecturally executed by the processor. EVENTBUS[16]: Stalls because instruction buffer cannot deliver an instruction. This can indicate an instruction cache miss. Asserted every cycle where the condition is present. EVENTBUS[19]: External memory request. Examples of this are cache refill, non-cacheable accesses, write-through writes, cache line evictions (write-back). EVENTBUS[20]: Stalls because of Load Store Unit (LSU) being busy. The event takes place each clock cycle where the condition is met. A high incidence of this event indicates the pipeline is often waiting for transactions to complete on the external bus. The unit ACTMON uses aon_cpu_clk as the refclk.
#### 9.13.3.4 Reset and Clocking
##### 9.13.3.4.1 Reset
There are several independent reset domains in the AON Cluster to be able to reset independently different parts of the Cortex-R5 and AON Cluster. Cortex-R5 Reset Cortex-R5 can start executing instructions as soon as its reset is released (deasserted). Hence, it is important to ensure that the entire system is ready to accept instructions before Cortex-R5 is released out of reset. Table 9.105 Cortex-R5 Reset Domains Reset Domain Description ACPRESETn Since Cortex-R5 subsystem doesn't have an ACP, this is tied inactive (to 1) nRESET CPU non-debug logic reset. Notes: Whenever nRESET is asserted, it should be asserted for at least four CLKIN cycles for correct reset operation. This is the signal that is pulsed by the watchdog timer on a "processor hang" if debug through reset is needed. nSYSPORESET Cortex-R5 system reset This resets the Cortex-R5 processor and debug logic. Note: Whenever nSYSPORESET is asserted, it should be asserted for at least four CLKIN cycles for correct reset operation. nPRESETDBG Cortex-R5 Debug reset. Resets debug-domain debug logic and the APB interface of the CPU.

AON Registers Reset Domain Description nCPUHALT Prevents the Cortex-R5 from fetching code out of reset. DBGRESETn Cortex-R5 Debug reset. Resets core-domain debug logic. This includes breakpoints, watchpoints, and the DCC registers. AON Cluster Reset There are four groups of resets in the AON cluster as shown in the table below. They are grouped so that the reset assertion and deassertion can be understood in terms of groups rather than a bunch of independent signals. Table 9.106 Reset Groups in AON Cluster Group 0 Group 1 Group 2 Group 3 System reset + All AON cluster resets, with the exception of Groups 1, 2, and 3 resets CAN1 and CAN2 reset nSYSPORRESET, VIC0, VIC1 nCPUHALT The order of deassertion of resets on cold boot is from Group 0 through Group 3. 1. Group 0 reset is the system reset. This reset is the system reset and is generated by PMC. This reset is the reset for most modules in the AON cluster. Group 1 reset is the Group 0 reset qualified by the fuses valid signal, straps valid signal and RAM valid signal. This reset goes to the CAN controllers. DBGRESETn, nPRESETDBG, and nRESET may be extended up to four clocks after the Group 1 reset deasserts. Group 2 reset group is primarily the Cortex-R5 Power-on-Reset and the PL192 resets. This is the last module in the AON cluster that comes out of reset. The rest of the cluster is ready to receive and process Cortex-R5 CPU's requests as soon as Cortex-R5 is released. The Group 2 reset is the same as Group 1 reset except it may be extended up to four clocks. Group 3 reset group includes the nCPUHALT. This isn't truly a processor reset, but can be used to hold processor from executing instructions. For the AON cluster nCPUHALT should remain asserted until firmware has been loaded into the TCM. To do this as FWLoadDone bit is set by the boot code once the TCM load is complete. The FWLoadDone bit is not cleared except by an aon_cluster_reset. 2. 3. 4.

Note that writing TMRCR with EN=1 while EN was already 1 restarts the counter. Parity Protection: N SCR Protection: TMRSCR2_0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bxx00,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 29:0 0x0 TARGET: Target value of the selected reference counter, i.e. when value of the selected reference equals target value, the interrupt is generated. The difference between TARGET and the current value must be positive when interpreting TARGET and the 29 LSB of the selected reference counter as signed integers, otherwise the interrupt triggers immediately. TKE_AON_TIMER_TMR3_TMRCR_0 Timer Configuration Register Offset: 0x40000 Read/Write: See table below. Parity Protection: N

AON Registers SCR Protection: TMRSCR3_0 Reset: 0x40000000 (0b01x0,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000) Bit Reset Description 0x0 EN: Enable, when set, enables the countdown process. 0x1 PER: Periodic, when set, the internal counter is automatically reloaded after reaching 0 28:0 0x0 PTV: Timer Present Trigger Value. When TMRCR is written and EN is 1b, the internal counter is loaded with PTV+1 and starts counting down at each timing reference pulse. An interrupt is set when the internal counter reaches 0. Note that writing TMRCR with EN=1 while EN was already 1 restarts the counter. Once the timer is started, TARGET can be used to either observe the value of the reference counter when the next interrupt is generated (read) or select the exact reference counter value at which the next interrupt is generated (write) TKE_AON_TIMER_TMR3_TMRSR_0 Timer Status Register Offset: 0x40004 Read/Write: See table below Parity Protection: N SCR Protection: TMRSCR3_0 Reset: 0x00000000 (0bx0x0,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000,0000) Bit R/W Reset Description RW 0x0 INTR_CLR: Clears the interrupt when written as 1b, read always returns 0 28:0 RO 0x0 PCV: Current counter value, writing to this field has no effect TKE_AON_TIMER_TMR3_TMRCSSR_0 Timer Clock Source Selection Register Offset: 0x40008 Read/Write: See table below.
